## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a population (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. Classical population dynamics models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex models with Allee effects, time-dependent carrying capacities, and oscillatory forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth/decline)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth with logarithmic density dependence)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**2 * (1 - c1 * P) (cooperative growth at low density)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent growth with proportional removal)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (growth with constant yield removal)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Richards growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized sigmoidal growth)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Beverton-Holt continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with density-dependent resource limitation)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (logistic with shifting capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence (self-limitation) → Polynomial in P: terms like P*(1 - c*P) or P*log(c/P) indicate intraspecific competition
- Allee effects (cooperative growth) → Cubic polynomials in P or P² leading terms indicate minimum population thresholds for positive growth
- Environmental periodicity → Multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth terms reflects seasonal forcing
- Harvesting or immigration → Additive constant terms (±c) independent of P represent external population inputs/removals
- Metabolic scaling → Fractional power terms P**c (where c ≠ 1) reflect allometric/metabolic scaling relationships in growth
- Carrying capacity structure → dP_dt = 0 when P equals a specific value, enforced by factor (1 - c*P) or similar zero-crossing terms
- Multiple equilibria → Products of multiple (P - c_i) factors indicate bistability or multiple steady states in population
- Quasi-periodic or aperiodic dynamics → Products of trigonometric functions with incommensurate frequencies sin(c1*t)*sin(c2*t)
- Delayed density feedback via time → Explicit t-dependence in growth rate can proxy for age-structure or delayed feedback effects

### Candidate 9:

**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 10:
`P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P**c3*c4*sin(c5*t + c6) + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)`

Has P*exp(t) ✓, P (linear), P^c3*sin(t), sin(t).
To get P^(1/3), we'd need P^c3*c4*sin(c5*t+c6) to be time-independent, but sin is always oscillating unless c5=0. If c5=0, then P^c3*c4*sin(c6). Set c3=1/3, this gives c4*sin(c6)*P^(1/3) which is a constant times P^(1/3) ✓. Set c7=0 and c2=0.

So: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P^(1/3)*c4*sin(c6) = matches GT with c0=0.4867, c1=-0.08577, c4*sin(c6)=0.4867.

**Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]**

No exp(-t) term. Cannot produce P*exp(-t).
